          traits requires a comprehensive approach that integrates genetic and

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Introduction section to enhance clarity, reduce
          jargon, and maintain a scholarly tone. The revision should adhere to
          Markdown formatting and follow a Context-Content-Conclusion (C-C-C)
          structure. This structure begins by setting the stage with one or two
          sentences (Context), progresses through what is known from the
          literature (Content), and concludes by highlighting an aspect of the
          knowledge gap the manuscript addresses (Conclusion). Your revision
          should: 1) preserve the original information as much as possible, with
          minimal changes to the text, 2) ensure most references to scientific
          articles are kept exactly as they appear in the original text; these
          references are crucial for academic integrity and may appear with the
          format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as "[@pmid:33931583;
          @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]", and 4) the revised
          paragraph must encapsulate the entire revision, following the C-C-C
          structure, within a single, cohesive paragraph.


          Input paragraph: Genes work together in context-specific networks to
          karry out different functions [@pmid:19104045; @doi:10.1038/ng.3259].
          Variations in these genes can change their functional role and, at a
          higher level, affect disease-relevant biological processes
          [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-06022-6]. In this context, determining how
          genes influence complex traits requires mechanistically understanding
          ekspression regulation across different cell types
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776; @doi:10.1038/s41586-020-2559-3;
          @doi:10.1038/s41576-019-0200-9], which in turn should lead to improved

          @doi:10.1038/nature12787; @doi:10.1038/s41586-020-03145-z;
          @doi:10.1038/s41586-020-2559-3] including genetic effects on gene

          dysregulated, commonly result in tissue- and cell lineage-specific
          pathology [@pmid:20624743; @pmid:14707169;
          @doi:10.1073/pnas.0810772105].

          [@doi:10.1186/s13059-021-02591-w] and drug repurposing
          [@doi:10.1038/nn.4618] tasks. However, TWAS works at the individual
          gene level, which does not capture more complex interactions at the
          network level.

          network level.

          genes interact to influence disease risk, is a challenging task.

          Given the wealth of gene expression data across multiple tissues, an
          effective approach to identify biological processes is the

          gene level, which does not capture more complex interactions at the
          network level. Therefore, while TWAS is a powerful tool for
          identifying disease-associated genes, it may not be as effective for
          identifying disease-associated networks.

          Gene expression data across multiple tissues provides a rich resource
          for unraveling the etiology and drug mechanisms of complex diseases.
          However, traditional GWAS approaches, which focus on single genes,

          whether perturbations in gene regulatory mechanisms mediate the

          individual gene level limits its ability to capture complex
          interactions at the network level. By employing TWAS, researchers can

          **Context:**

          The field of genetic research has made significant strides in
          identifying genetic variants associated with complex diseases,
          including cancer and drug resistance. However, existing approaches,

          facilitates the discovery of novel therapeutic targets and drug

          novel therapeutic strategies. By bridging the gap between individual
          gene and network-level approaches, this study paves the way for a more
          comprehensive understanding of complex diseases and the development of
          personalized treatments.

          ## Integrating gene co-expression and functional genomics for disease
          etiology and drug repurposing.


          Despite the wealth of genetic data, identifying the biological
          processes underlying complex diseases remains a significant challenge.
          While traditional GWAS approaches have proven successful in uncovering
          disease etiology at the single-gene level, they fail to capture the
          intricate interactions occurring at the network level. This is
          particularly relevant in diseases with multiple genetic causes, where
          a single genetic variant may be implicated in disease development
          through diverse pathways.


          By integrating expression quantitative trait loci (eQTLs) data into
          GWAS, we can leverage the strengths of both approaches. This approach
          provides a mechanistic interpretation for GWAS findings by identifying
          the co-expression of genes in disease-associated pathways. This
          information can guide the discovery of novel therapeutic targets and
          drug repurposing opportunities.

              **Context:** 

              Gene expression data across multiple tissues provides a rich
              resource for unraveling the etiology and drug mechanisms of
              complex diseases. However, traditional GWAS approaches, which
              focus on single genes, fail to capture the intricate interplay of
              genetic variants and biological processes that contribute to
              disease susceptibility.


              **Content:**

              The advent of high-throughput technologies has revolutionized our
              ability to study gene expression at a global scale. This has led
              to the development of powerful tools for integrating expression
              quantitative trait loci (eQTLs) data into GWAS analysis. These
              methods provide a mechanistic interpretation for GWAS findings by
              testing whether perturbations in gene regulatory mechanisms
              mediate the association between genetic variants and diseases.


              **Conclusion:**

              The application of TWAS has significantly advanced our
              understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms. However,
              its focus on the individual gene level limits its ability to
              capture complex interactions at the network level. By employing

              **Context:**

              The field of genetic research has made significant strides in
              identifying genetic variants associated with complex diseases,
              including cancer and drug resistance. However, existing
              approaches, such as transcription-wide association studies (TWAS),
              have limitations in capturing the intricate interplay between
              genetic variants and disease risk.


              **Content:**

              This manuscript presents a novel approach to address this
              limitation by leveraging the power of gene expression data. By
              integrating information from gene co-expression networks, we gain
              a mechanistic understanding of genetic associations beyond the
              individual gene level. This approach, termed clustering of complex
              traits (CCT), facilitates the discovery of novel therapeutic
              targets and drug repurposing opportunities.


              **Conclusion:**

              The inclusion of gene expression data in the analysis framework
              offers a powerful means to elucidate the etiology of diseases and
              identify novel therapeutic strategies. By bridging the gap between
              individual gene and network-level approaches, this study paves the
              way for a more comprehensive understanding of complex diseases and
              the development of personalized treatments.
